Distinction Between Quantity (Asl) and Description (Wasf) in Sales
Defines the distinction between asl and wasf in sales.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between quantity (asl) and description (wasf) in sales and apply the Hanafi ruling for excess/deficiency in length-measured goods.

Core Idea
In Hanafi sales, quantity in measured/weighed goods is principle (asl) but length in cloth is description (wasf) – affecting remedies for excess/deficiency.

This lesson from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq clarifies a critical distinction in Hanafi sales law: the difference between the object's quantity and its description. Understanding this distinction determines who bears the risk of measurement errors and what remedies are available to the buyer and seller.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of goods
The passage distinguishes between goods measured by volume/weight (makilat/mawzunat) and goods measured by length (madhru'at). In the first, quantity is asl; in the second, length is wasf.
This categorization is key to applying the correct ruling.
2
Extract the Hanafi definitions of asl and wasf
From the three definitions given by the mashayikh, determine that asl is that which does not impair the remainder when lost, while wasf is that whose loss decreases the value of the remainder.
These definitions are found in the latter part of the passage.
3
Apply the wasf ruling to length goods
For cloth (madhru'), deficiency gives the buyer the option to take at full price or cancel; excess belongs to the buyer and the seller has no option. This is the core rule from the matn commentary.
This contrasts with the rule for asl where proportional adjustment may apply.
4
Note additional consequences (thamarat)
The passage lists practical fruits: (a) a buyer may dispose of length goods before measuring but not measured goods before weighing; (b) selling one for two (e.g., two lengths as a set) is permissible for length goods but not for measured goods.
These illustrate the legal effect of the asl/wasf distinction.
5
Contrast with other schools
The Hanafi position that length is wasf may differ from other schools that treat length as asl, leading to different remedies (e.g., proportional reduction for deficiency).
This sharpens the understanding of the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية : عد الكواغد فظنها أربعة وعشرين وأخبر البائع به ثم أضاف العقد إلى عينها ولم يذكر العدد ثم ازدادت على ما ظنه فهي حلال للمشتري. وفي فتاوى صاعد: ساومه الحنطة كل قفيز بثمن معين وحاسبوا فبلغ ستمائة درهم فغلطوا وحاسبوا المشتري بخمسمائة وباعوها منه بخمسمائة ثم ظهر أن فيها غلطاً لا يلزمه إلا خمسمائة . أفرز القصاب أربع شياه فقال بائعها هي بخمسة كل واحدة فذهب القصاب فجاء بأربع دنانير فقال للبائع هل بعت هذه بهذا القدر والبائع أنه يعتقد أنها خمسة؟ قال: صح البيع . قال رضي الله تعالى عنه : وهذا إشارة إلى بأربعة يصح ولا يعتبر ما سبق أن كل واحدة بدينار وربع اهـ . (فرع) لطيف من أيمان خزانة الفتاوى مناسب للوزنيات: اشترى مناً من اللحم فقالت هذا أقل من من وحلفت عليه وقال الزوج إن لم يكن مناً فأنت طالق فالحيلة فيه أن يطبخ قبل أن يوزن فلا يحنثان اهـ قوله : (وإن نقص ذراع أخذ بكل الثمن أو ترك وإن زاد فللمشترى ولا خيار للبائع) لأن الذرع في المذروع وصف لأنه عبارة عن الطول فيه لكنه وصف يستلزم زيادة أجزاء فإن لم يفرد بثمن كان تابعاً محضاً فلا يقابل بشيء من الثمن، فإذا قال على أنها مائة ذراع بمائة ولم يزد فوجدها أنقص كان عليه جميع الثمن، وإنما يتخير لفوات الوصف المشروط المرغوب فيه كما إذا اشتراه على أنه كاتب فوجده غير كاتب، وإن وجدها أزيد فللمشتري الزيادة ولا خيار للبائع كما إذا باعه على أنه معيب فإذا هو سليم، وقد ذكر المشايخ في التفريق بين القدر وهو الأصل والوصف حدوداً فقيل ما يتعيب بالتبعيض والتشقيص فالزيادة والنقصان فيه وصف، وما لا يتعيب بهما فالزيادة والنقصان فيه أصل . وقيل : الوصف ما لوجوده تأثير في تقوم غيره ولعدمه تأثير في نقصان غيره، والأصل ما لا يكون بهذه المثابة . وقيل : ما لا ينقص بالباقي لفواته فهو أصل وما ينقص الباقي بفواته فهو وصف وهذا مع الثاني متقاربان فبهذا علم أن القدر في المكيلات والموزونات أصل والذرع في المذروعات وصف وثمرة كون الذرع وصفاً والقدر أصلاً تظهر في مواضع منها ما ذكر في الكتاب ومنها أنه لا يجوز للمشتري التصرف في المبيع قبل الكيل والوزن إذا اشتراه بشرط الكيل والوزن ويجوز به في المذروع قبل الذرع، سواء اشتراه مجازفة أو بشرط الذرع ومنها أن بيع الواحد باثنين لا يجوز في المكيلات والموزونات ويجوز في المذروعات؛ كذا في المعراج إلا إذا بين لكل ذراع ثمناً فإنه لا يتصرف
And in al-Qunyah: If he counted papers and thought they were twenty-four and informed the seller, then he attached the contract to the specific item without mentioning the number, and then they increased more than what he thought, it is permissible (halal) for the buyer. And in Fatawa Sa'id: He bargained with him for wheat, each qafiz at a specific price, and they calculated and it reached six hundred dirhams, they made a mistake and calculated with the buyer five hundred and sold it to him for five hundred, then it became apparent there was an error; he is not obliged to pay more than five hundred. The butcher set aside four sheep, and the seller said they are five for each one, so the butcher went and came with four dinars and said to the seller, 'Did you sell these for this amount?' while the seller believed they were five? He said: 'The sale is valid.' Radi Allahu 'anhu said: This indicates that the sale is valid for four, and no consideration is given to the previous statement that each one was for a dinar and a quarter. A subtle branch from Ayman Khizanat al-Fatawa relevant to weight-based sales: If a man bought a mann of meat, and his wife said 'This is less than a mann' and she swore to it, and the husband said 'If it is not a mann, you are divorced,' the stratagem is to cook it before weighing, so neither is guilty of perjury. He said: (And if it is deficient by a cubit, he takes it for the whole price or leaves it, and if it is extra, it belongs to the buyer, and the seller has no option) because the length in goods measured by length is a description (wasf), as it expresses the length in them, but it is a description that entails an increase in parts. If it is not given a separate price, it is purely a follow, so it is not compensated by any part of the price. So if he said 'on the condition that it is a hundred cubits for a hundred' and did not elaborate, and found it less, he is liable for the whole price, but he has an option due to the loss of the stipulated desirable description, just as if he bought it on the condition that he is a writer and found him not a writer. And if he found it extra, the increase belongs to the buyer and the seller has no option, just as if he sold it on the condition it is defective and it turned out sound. The mashayikh have mentioned boundaries in distinguishing between quantity (qadr) which is the principle (asl) and description (wasf). It is said: that which is impaired by division and partitioning such that increase and decrease in it is description, and that which is not impaired by them is principle. It is said: Description is that whose existence affects the value of others and whose absence affects the decrease of others; principle is not like that. It is said: That which does not cause the remainder to decrease upon its loss is principle, and that which causes the remainder to decrease upon its loss is description. This is close to the second. By this it is known that quantity in measured-by-volume and weighed goods is principle, and length in goods measured by length is description. The fruits of length being description and quantity being principle appear in several places: among them what is mentioned in the book, and among them that it is not permissible for the buyer to dispose of the sold item before measurement and weighing if he bought it with the condition of measurement and weighing, but it is permissible for him to dispose of goods measured by length before measuring, whether he bought them by guess or with the condition of measuring. And among them that selling one for two is not permissible in measured-by-volume and weighed goods, but is permissible in goods measured by length. This is in al-Mi'raj, unless he specified a price for each cubit, then he may not dispose.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion that synthesizes the previous discussions. It opens with two fatwas from al-Qunyah and Fatawa Sa'id: one about counting papers without specifying number (increase is permissible), and another about a mistaken calculation in a wheat sale (buyer pays only the agreed amount). Then a stratagem from Khizanat al-Fatawa: in an oath case about meat weight, cooking before weighing avoids breaking the oath. The core of the lesson is the commentary on the matn statement about length-measured goods: if a fabric is found longer or shorter than stated, the ruling differs from measured/weighed goods. The author explains that length (adhr'u') in goods measured by length (madhr'uat) is a description (wasf), not principle (asl). Therefore, deficiency gives the buyer the option to take the whole at full price or cancel, but excess goes to the buyer without the seller having an option. The mashayikh have various definitions for distinguishing asl from wasf: (1) what is impaired by division is wasf; (2) what affects the value of others is wasf; (3) what does not decrease the remainder upon loss is asl. Applying these, quantity in makilat/mawzunat is asl, while length in madhru'at is wasf. Practical consequences: (a) a buyer cannot dispose of measured goods before measurement, but can dispose of length goods before measuring; (b) selling one for two (like selling two lengths at once) is allowed for length goods but not for measured ones.

Key Terms
أصل (aṣl): The principle or foundation of the sold item; quantity in makilat/mawzunat.
وصف (waṣf): A description or attribute of the item; length in madhru'at is wasf.
مذروع (madhru‘): Goods measured by length, such as cloth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, a buyer purchases a piece of cloth on condition it is 10 cubits. He finds it is 11 cubits. What is the ruling?
A) The seller may void the sale.
B) The extra cubit belongs to the buyer and the seller has no option.
C) The sale is void because the condition is not met.
D) The buyer must pay extra for the additional cubit.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, quantity in measured/weighed goods is the principal (asl), but length in cloth is a description (wasf), so remedies for over- or under-delivery differ fundamentally.

Ruling on Shortfall or Excess in Sale by Measurement
Commentary on the matn rule for measured items when actual size differs from stated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a sold item measured by cubit is found to be short or in excess, and explain the legal reasoning based on the distinction between asl and wasf.

Core Idea
In a sale by cubit, measurement is a description (wasf), not essence; shortfall gives option to pay full or cancel, excess is buyer's gain.

This commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq explains the rule for items sold by cubit measurement (madhru‘). The key is understanding that the cubit measurement is a description (wasf), not the essence (asl) of the sold item. This distinction determines the options of the parties when the actual measurement differs from what was stated. We will walk through the ruling, its proof by analogy, and the practical consequences that flow from this classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for shortfall
If the item is short by a cubit, the buyer must either take it at the full price or cancel the sale. There is no proportional reduction.
The buyer's option is due to loss of a stipulated desirable description (khiyar al-wasf).
2
Identify the ruling for excess
If the item is more than stated, the extra belongs to the buyer and the seller has no option to cancel or claim extra price.
The seller's silence is analogous to selling a defective item that turns out sound.
3
Understand the reasoning: measurement is a wasf
The cubit measurement expresses length, which is a quality that can increase or decrease without affecting the essence. As a pure description, it does not correspond to a portion of the price.
Analogies: buying a slave described as a writer (wasf) vs. buying grains by weight (asl).
4
Examine the definitions of asl vs. wasf
Scholars define: if division or partitioning causes defect, measurement is a description (wasf); if not, it is essence (asl). Other definitions relate to effect on value.
5
Apply the consequences
Because the cubit is a wasf, the buyer may dispose of the item before measurement, and selling one for two is permissible for madhru‘ items but not for weighed/measured items.
This practical fruit (thamarah) shows the wide-ranging impact of the classification.

His statement: (And if it is short by a cubit, he takes it at the full price or leaves it, and if it is more, it belongs to the buyer and there is no option for the seller) because the cubit measurement in measured items is a description, since it expresses the length in it, but it is a description that entails an increase in parts. If it is not assigned a separate price, it is a pure follow-up, so nothing of the price corresponds to it. If he finds it more, the increase belongs to the buyer and there is no option for the seller, as if he sold it on condition that it is defective but it turns out sound. And it is said: description is that whose existence affects the value of something else and whose absence affects a decrease in something else; essence is not like that. And it is said: what does not decrease the remainder by its absence is essence, and what decreases the remainder by its absence is description. This is close to the second. Thus it is known that quantity in weighed and measured items is essence, and the cubit in measured items is description. Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author explains the ruling when a sold item measured by cubit (dhira) is found to be short or in excess of the stated measurement. He begins by stating the core rule: if the item is short, the buyer must pay the full price or cancel; if it is in excess, the extra belongs to the buyer and the seller has no option. The reason is that the cubit measurement is a 'description' (wasf), not the 'essence' (asl) of the sold item. As a description, it is subsidiary and not assigned a portion of the price. The author then clarifies by comparing to other conditions: if a buyer stipulates a writer but finds him illiterate, he has the option. Similarly, if the seller indicates a defect but it turns out sound, the buyer benefits. The scholars have given several definitions to distinguish between quantity (asl) and description. The key distinction is that in items where division or partitioning causes defect, the measurement is a description; in items that are not defective by division (like grains and weights), the quantity is the essence. The practical consequences (thamarat) are explained: for measured items, the buyer may dispose before measurement; for weighed/measured items, he cannot before weighing/measuring. Also, selling one for two is impermissible in weight/measure items but permissible in measured items (since the cubit is a description). The author also notes exceptions when each cubit is priced separately, and mentions that sawiq (a type of parched barley) and soap are value-based due to significant quality differences. This lesson is essential for understanding how the Hanafi school classifies properties as 'asl' or 'wasf' in sales transactions, a distinction with wide-ranging legal effects.

Key Terms
وصف (wasf): A quality or attribute that is not independently valuable and does not correspond to a portion of the price; it is subsidiary to the essence.
أصل (asl): The primary subject matter of the sale; its quantity or substance that has intrinsic value and corresponds to the price proportionally.
مذروع (madhru'): An item sold by measurement in cubits (dhira'), such as cloth or land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He may deduct the shortfall proportionally from the price.
B) He must pay the full price or cancel the sale.
C) He may reduce the price by the value of the missing part.
D) He automatically gets the shortage free of charge.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the cubit measurement in a sale is a description (wasf), not essence; a shortfall gives only the option to cancel or pay full price, and excess belongs to the buyer without seller's recourse.

Sale by Each Cubit with Separate Price: Options for Shortfall and Excess
Ruling when each cubit is priced individually: different consequences for shortfall/excess

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the buyer's options when each cubit is priced separately and explain the dual nature (asl/wasf) that justifies the ruling.

Core Idea
Per-unit pricing makes each unit an 'asl': shortfall gives refund option, excess must be paid.

This lesson explores a unique Hanafi ruling on sales where each unit is priced individually. The key insight is that assigning a price to a measurement transforms it from a mere description (wasf) into an independent essence (asl), yet it retains some descriptive nature. This dual character leads to nuanced options for the buyer when the actual amount differs from what was stated. The passage also addresses an objection based on combined existence and non-existence, and provides a sophisticated response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Determine what the seller said ('each cubit for such-and-such') and whether the contract is valid. The Hanafi position is that the contract is valid (sahih).
2
Understand the key distinction: ifrad (assigning price per unit)
When each cubit is given a separate price, the cubit ceases to be a mere description and becomes an essence (asl). This is the foundation for the different treatment of shortfall and excess.
Without ifrad, the measurement remains a description and different rules apply (covered in previous lessons).
3
Trace the reasoning for shortfall vs excess
For shortfall: the buyer may take a proportionate refund or cancel, because paying the full price would not correspond to the priced units. For excess: the buyer may take the extra at its share or cancel, because the excess is not automatically given due to its asl nature.
The rule balances the buyer's rights and prevents harm.
4
Analyze the objection and the Hanafi response
An objection is raised: combining existing and non-existing should invalidate the contract, akin to buying two garments and finding a different one. The response: the cubit is both asl and wasf, so the contract remains valid for shortfall while preventing free excess.
This dual nature is the key: from one perspective it is an essence, from another a description.
5
Apply the principle to other cases
The rule is limited to when the price is explicitly assigned per unit. Without explicit assignment, the measurement remains a description and different rulings (e.g., from earlier parts) apply.
The last part of the passage emphasizes that the dual nature is resolved by explicit assignment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال كل ذراع بكذا ونقص ذراع أخذ بحصته أو ترك وإن زاد أخذ كله كل ذراع بكذا أو فسخ لما قدمنا أنه وإن كان وصفاً إذا أفرد بثمن صار أصلاً وارتفع عن التبعية فنزل كل ذراع منزلة ثوب، فإذا وجدها ناقصة خير لأنه لو أخذها بكل الثمن لم يكن آخذاً كل ذراع بدرهم، ولو وجدها زائدة لم تسلم له لصيرورتها أصلاً فخير بين أن يأخذ الزائد بحصته وبين أن يفسخ لرفع الضرر عن التزام الزائد وأورد عليه : ينبغي فساد العقد في صورة النقصان عند أبي حنيفة قولي الشافعي للجمع بين الموجود والمعدوم كما إذا اشترى ثوبين هرويين فإذا مروي . وأجيب بأن الذرع وإن صار أصلاً بإفراد الثمن هو وصف حقيقة فكان أصلاً من وجه دون وجه، فمن حيث إنه أصل لا تسلم له الزيادة، ومن حيث إنه وصف لم يفسد العقد فيما إذا وجد ناقصاً بخلاف تلك المسألة فإن الثوبين أصل من وجه. وبهذا الجواب اندفع ما أورد أنه من ينبغي أن يكون أصلاً وإن لم يفرد لكل ذراع ثمن لأنه لما قابل عشرة بعشرة مثلاً انقسم الآحاد على الآحاد فيصير بسبب المقابلة كأنه أفرد وحاصل الجواب أنه لما اجتمع فيه الأصالة والوصفية جعلناه أصلاً عند الإفراد ووصفاً عند تركه صريحاً عملاً
And if he said 'each cubit for such-and-such' and it is short by a cubit, he takes its share or leaves, and if it is more, he takes all of it each cubit for such-and-such, or he cancels. Because we have mentioned that although it is a description, when it is assigned a price, it becomes an essence and rises from subordination, so each cubit becomes like a garment. So if he finds it short, he has the option, because if he took it at the full price, he would not be taking each cubit for a dirham. And if he finds it more, the extra is not given to him because it has become an essence, so he has the option between taking the extra at its share and cancelling, to remove the harm of committing to the extra. An objection was raised: the contract should be invalid in the case of shortfall according to Abu Hanifa and the two views of al-Shafi'i, due to combining the existing and non-existent, as if he bought two Herawi garments and found one Marwi. And it was answered that even though the cubit becomes an essence by assigning a price, it is still a description in reality, so it is an essence from one perspective and not from another. From the perspective that it is an essence, the extra is not given to him; from the perspective that it is a description, the contract is not invalidated when it is short, unlike that issue where the two garments are essences from one perspective. With this answer, the objection that it should be an essence even if he did not assign a price for each cubit is repelled, because when he matched ten with ten, the units are divided against units, so due to the matching it becomes as if he assigned. The gist of the answer is that when both essence and description are combined in it, we make it an essence when explicitly assigned and a description when left unassigned, acting accordingly.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage discusses a variation of the previous ruling: when the seller explicitly prices each individual cubit (e.g., 'each cubit for 1 dirham'), the cubit measurement transforms from a mere description (wasf) to an essence (asl) because it is assigned a specific price. Consequently, the legal effects differ: if the actual measurement is less than stated, the buyer may either pay only for the actual cubits (i.e., take a proportionate refund) or cancel the contract. If the measurement is more, the buyer must either pay for the extra at the stated per-cubit price or cancel; he does not get the extra for free. The author notes an objection: according to Abu Hanifa and a view of al-Shafi'i, combining something that exists (the actual cubits) with something that does not (the missing cubits) should invalidate the contract, similar to buying two specific garments and one being different. The answer is that the cubit measurement is both an essence (because priced) and a description (by its nature). This duality prevents invalidation of the contract for shortfall (since it remains a description in part), but also prevents the buyer from taking excess for free (since it is an essence). The author concludes that when price is assigned per unit, it is treated as essence; when not assigned, it remains a pure description. This nuanced distinction is characteristic of Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
أصل (asl): In this context, when a component is assigned a separate price, it becomes an 'asl' meaning it has independent value and its shortage/excess must be compensated proportionally.
أفراد بثمن (ifrad bi-thaman): Assigning a specific price to each unit (e.g., each cubit for 1 dirham), which elevates the unit from description to essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Pay only for the actual cubits (proportionate refund) or cancel.
B) Pay the full price and keep the cloth.
C) Get the shortage for free.
D) The contract is automatically void.

Key Takeaway
When each unit is priced separately, the measurement becomes an essence for the extra but remains a description for the deficiency — resulting in a valid contract with proportional options.

Selling by the Cubit: Description vs. Principal in Hanafi Sales
Ruling on selling by cubit with variable quantity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a sale is made at a price per cubit and the actual quantity differs, and explain the reasoning based on the distinction between description (waṣf) and principal (aṣl).

Core Idea
When a per-unit price is specified, each unit becomes a principal; surplus goes to buyer only if they pay extra or cancel.

In Hanafi sales law, selling by the cubit with a per-unit price creates a special situation. The cubit is ordinarily a description (waṣf), but when individually priced, it becomes a principal (aṣl). This transformation determines the buyer's options if the actual quantity differs from the estimated one. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical rulings, including extensions to weighed and manufactured goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The matn states: if the buyer specifies a price per cubit and the quantity is short, the buyer may take it at a reduced price or cancel; if there is surplus, the buyer may take all at the per-unit price or cancel. This is the foundational ruling.
The buyer never automatically gains or loses; options preserve fairness.
2
Understand the waṣf vs. aṣl distinction
The commentator explains that the cubit is a description (waṣf) but when assigned a separate price, it becomes a principal (aṣl). This shift from subordination to independence is the key legal reasoning (ta'lil).
Aṣl = independent component; waṣf = incidental attribute.
3
Apply the reasoning to surplus and shortfall
In surplus, because the extra cubits are now independent, they do not automatically belong to the buyer; the buyer has a choice to take them at the per-unit price or cancel. In shortfall, the buyer may either pay for the existing cubits (proportional price) or cancel, because paying the full price would violate the per-unit agreement.
The duality of waṣf and aṣl prevents the contract from being corrupt.
4
Examine objections and responses
An objection arises: shouldn't the contract be invalid in shortfall, like selling two specified cloths that turn out to be different? The answer: the cubit retains some descriptiveness; it is a principal only when priced, so shortfall does not corrupt the contract.
This distinguishes from cases where the subject matter is entirely different.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on qada' vs. diyanah
Some Hanafi authorities (Qadi Khan) hold that the increase is given to the buyer only judicially (qada'), not religiously (diyanah). The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the buyer takes the increase in qada' and diyanah, but the ikhtilaf is legitimate.
This reflects different weights given to apparent vs. inner justice.

وإن زاد فللمشتري» أن الزيادة تسلم له قضاء وديانة، وحكى خلافاً فيه في المعراج فقال في فتاوى النسفي وأما لي قاضيخان : لا تسلم له الزيادة ديانة. وفي شرح أبي ذر والجامع الأصغر عن أسد وأبي حفص وأبي الليث : لا يردها ديانة. وفي العمدة لو اشترى حطباً على أنه عشرون وقراً فوجده ثلاثين طابت له الزيادة كما في الذرعان .اهـ. وفرع الحطب مشكل، وينبغي أن يكون من قبيل القدر لأنه لا يتعيب بالتبعيض فينبغي أن تكون الزيادة للبائع خصوصاً إن كان من الطرفاء التي تعورف وزنها بالقاهرة. وفي الخانية : رجل قال أبيعك هذا الثوب من هذا الطرف إلى هذا الطرف وهو ثلاثة عشر ذراعاً فإذا هو خمسة عشر فقال البائع غلطت لا يلتفت إليه ويكون الثوب للمشتري بالثمن المسمى قضاء وفي الديانة لا تسلم له الزيادة اهـ قوله : (ولو قال كل ذراع بكذا ونقص أخذ حصتها أو ترك وإن زاد أخذ كله كل ذراع بكذا أو فسخ) لما قدمنا أنه وإن كان وصفاً إذا أفرد بثمن صار أصلاً وارتفع عن التبعية فنزل كل ذراع منزلة ثوب، فإذا وجدها ناقصة خير لأنه لو أخذها بكل الثمن لم يكن آخذاً كل ذراع بدرهم، ولو وجدها زائدة لم تسلم له لصيرورتها أصلاً فخير بين أن يأخذ الزائد بحصته وبين أن يفسخ لرفع الضرر عن التزام الزائد وأورد عليه : ينبغي فساد العقد في صورة النقصان عند أبي حنيفة قولي الشافعي للجمع بين الموجود والمعدوم كما إذا اشترى ثوبين هرويين فإذا مروي [؟] . وأجيب بأن الذرع وإن صار أصلاً بإفراد الثمن هو وصف حقيقة فكان أصلاً من وجه دون وجه، فمن حيث إنه أصل لا تسلم له الزيادة، ومن حيث إنه وصف لم يفسد العقد فيما إذا وجد ناقصاً بخلاف تلك المسألة فإن الثوبين أصل من وجه. وبهذا الجواب اندفع ما أورد أنه من ينبغي أن يكون أصلاً وإن لم يفرد لكل ذراع ثمن لأنه لما قابل عشرة بعشرة مثلاً انقسم الآحاد على الآحاد فيصير بسبب المقابلة كأنه أفرد وحاصل الجواب أنه لما اجتمع فيه الأصالة والوصفية جعلناه أصلاً عند الإفراد ووصفاً عند تركه صريحاً عملاً كما أحد هو أحدهما [؟] بكذا أو فسخ وفسد بيع عشرة أذرع من دار لا أسهم ومن اشترى عدلاً على أنه عشرة بالشبهين؛ كذا في المعراج. وأورد أيضاً على القول بأصالته عند إفراد ثمنه لزوم امتناع دخول الزيادة في العقد كما في الصبرة مع أنكم جوزتم أخذ الجميع بحكم البيع. وأجيب عنه للفرق بينهما وهو أن الزيادة لو لم تدخل في العقد فسد لأنه يصير بعض الثوب، وأنه لا يجوز بخلاف الصبرة لأنها لو لم تدخل لم يفسد العقد كما في الفوائد الظهيرية. أطلق في المذروع فشمل الثوب والأرض والحطب والدار، فلو قال بعتك هذه الأرض على أنها ألف ذراع بألف فوجدها زائدة أو ناقصة فالبيع صحيح وله الزيادة بلا خيار وله الخيار مع النقصان . وإن أفرد لكل ذراع ثمناً . خير في صورة الزيادة وسقطت حصة النقصان ؛ كذا في البدائع. قال: وعلى هذا الموزونات التي في تبعيضها ضرر بأن قال بعت منك هذه السبيكة من الذهب على أنها مثقالان بكذا جاز البيع، فإن وجدها أزيد أو أنقص فهو كالمذروعات، وكذا إذا باع مصوغاً من نحاس أو صفر فهو على هذا التفصيل المذكور لأن الوزن في مثله يكون ملحقاً بالصفة لأن تبعيضه يوجب تعييب الباقي وهذا حد الصفة. ولو باع مصوغاً من الفضة وزنه مائة بدنانير ولم يسم لكل عشرة ثمناً على حدة وتقابضا جاز، فإن وجده أزيد فالكل للمشتري، وإن وجده أقل لكل عشرة ثمناً على حدة بأن قال وكل وزن عشرة بدينار، فإن وجده أزيد، خير، وإن سمى فإن علم قبل التفرق خير إن شاء زاد في الثمن وإن شاء ترك. وإن علم بعده بطل بقدر الزيادة وله الخيار فيما بقي لأن الشركة فيه عيب، وإن وجده ناقصاً خير قبل التفرق وبعده إن شاء وإن شاء رضي به بقسطه من الثمن. وكذا لو باع مصوغاً من ذهب بدراهم فهو على هذا التفصيل، ولو باع مصوغاً بجنسه مثل وزنه فوجده أزيد فإن علم بها قبل التفرق فله الخيار إن شاء زاد في الثمن قدرها وإن شاء ،ترك، وإن علم بها بعد التفرق بطل لفقد القبض في قدرها، وإن وجده أقل فله الخيار إن شاء رضي به واسترد الفضل وإن شاء رد الكل، سواء سمى لكل وزن درهم درهماً أو لا، لأن عند اتحاد الجنس لا بد من المساواة اهـ. وفي دعوى البزازية : ادعى زندبيجاً طوله بذرعان خوارزم كذا وشهدا بذلك كذلك بحضرة الزندبيجي فذرع فإذا هو أزيد أو أنقص بطلت الشهادة والدعوى كما إذا خالف سن الدابة الدعوى أو الشهادة. وقولهم الذرع وصف فيلغو في الحاضر ذلك في الأثمان والبيع لا في الدعوى والشهادة فإنهما إذا شهدا بوصف فظهر بخلافه لم يقبل . وذكر أيضاً : ادعى حديداً مشاراً إليه وذكر أنه عشرة أمناء فإذا هو عشرون أو ثمانية تقبل الدعوى والشهادة لأن الوزن في المشار إليه لغو اهـ
If he said: each cubit for such and such, and a cubit is missing, he takes its proportional share or leaves; if it is more, he takes all, each cubit before cubiting as in al-Muhit. And in it: description is not matched by anything from the price, like if the sold item becomes defective in the seller's hand before delivery, nothing of the price is dropped; similarly if it becomes defective in the buyer's hand, he may sell on profit without disclosure, unless it is intended for consumption in reality or by ruling. As for in reality, like if the seller cuts the slave's hand before taking possession, then half the price drops because it became intended for cutting; and by ruling, like if returning is prevented due to the seller's right, as when the sold item becomes defective with the buyer, or due to Sharia right, as if the sold item was a cloth and then a defect was found in it. When description is intended by one of these two ways, it takes a portion of the price; thus in al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyyah and in Idah al-Islah: what is meant by description is not what entails goodness or ugliness; what clarifies this is their statement: weight in what is harmed by division is description, and in what is not harmed, it is quantity with no difference in goodness or ugliness. End. And the apparent meaning of his statement 'if it is more, for the buyer' is that the increase is given to him judicially and religiously; and a difference was reported in al-Mi'raj, and he said in Fatawa al-Nasafi and by Qadi Khan: the increase is not given to him religiously. In Sharh Abi Dharr and al-Jami' al-Saghir from Asad, Abu Hafs, and Abu Layth: he does not return it religiously. In al-Umdah: if he bought wood on that it is twenty loads and found it thirty, the increase is permissible for him as in the two cubits. End. And the branch of wood is problematic; it should be of the type of quantity because it is not harmed by division, so the increase should be for the seller, especially if it is from [؟] which is customarily weighed in Cairo. In al-Khaniyyah: a man said: I sell you this cloth from this edge to this edge, and it is thirteen cubits, but it turned out to be fifteen; the seller said: I made a mistake; it is not heeded, and the cloth is for the buyer for the named price judicially, and religiously the increase is not given to him. End. His statement: (If he said each cubit for such and such, and it is short, he takes its share or leaves; if it is more, he takes all, each cubit for such and such or annuls.) Because we said that even if it is a description, when it is assigned a price individually it becomes a principal and rises from subordination, so each cubit is treated like a cloth; if he finds it short, he has a choice because if he took it for the full price, he wouldn't be taking each cubit for a dirham; if he finds it more, it is not given to him due to becoming a principal, so he has a choice between taking the increase for its portion and annulling to remove the harm of committing to the increase. An objection was raised: it would imply corruption of the contract in the case of shortfall according to Abu Hanifa and the two views of al-Shafi'i because of combining what exists and what does not, like if he bought two Herawi cloths and they turned out to be Marwi [؟]. The answer is that the cubit, even though it becomes a principal by assigning a price individually, is actually a description, so it is a principal from one aspect and not from another; from the aspect that it is a principal, the increase is not given to him; from the aspect that it is a description, the contract does not become corrupt when found short, unlike that case where the two cloths are principal from one aspect. With this answer, what was objected is repelled: that it would be appropriate that it be a principal even if no price is assigned for each cubit because when he matched ten with ten, for example, units divide onto units, so due to the correspondence it is as if he assigned individually. The summary of the answer is: since both principality and description are combined in it, we make it a principal at the time of individual assignment and a description at the time of explicit omission, acting [؟] as one of them is the other [؟]. With such and such or annul, and the sale of ten cubits from a house without shares is corrupt; and whoever buys a bundle on that it is ten and finds it more: with the two similarities; as in al-Mi'raj. Another objection was raised on the view of its principality when its price is assigned individually: the necessity of preventing the increase from entering the contract, as in the heap, even though you allowed taking the whole by virtue of the sale. The answer is the difference between them: that if the increase did not enter the contract, it would be corrupt because it becomes part of the cloth, and it is not permissible, unlike the heap because if it did not enter, the contract would not be corrupt as in al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyyah. He gave an absolute ruling in al-madhru' (measured by length) covering cloth, land, wood, and house; so if he said: I sell you this land on that it is a thousand cubits for a thousand, and he finds it more or less, the sale is valid and he takes the increase without choice, and he has choice with the shortfall. And if he assigned a price for each cubit, he has choice in the case of increase and the share of the shortfall drops; as in al-Bada'i. He said: and similarly items weighed where division harms them, by saying: I sold you this ingot of gold on that it is two mithqals for such and such, the sale is valid; if he finds it more or less, it is like the measured items; similarly if he sold manufactured goods of copper or brass, it is according to this detail because weight in such cases is attached to the description because its division necessitates defect in the remainder, and this is the definition of description. And if he sold manufactured goods of silver weighing a hundred for dinars and did not specify a price for each ten separately, and they took possession, it is valid; if he finds it more, all is for the buyer; if he finds it less [the text continues] If he specified a price for each ten separately by saying 'and each weight of ten for a dinar', then if he finds it more, he has a choice; if he specified, and he knew before separation, he chooses whether to increase the price or leave; if he knew after, it becomes void to the extent of the increase and he has the choice regarding the remainder because partnership in it is a defect; if he finds it short, he has a choice before and after separation: if he wishes, and if he wishes, he may accept it for its share of the price. Similarly, if he sold manufactured gold for silver, it is according to this detail. And if he sold manufactured goods for like kind, similar in weight, and finds it more: if he knew before separation, he has the choice to increase the price by its amount or leave; if he knew after separation, it becomes void due to lack of possession in its amount; if he finds it less, he has the choice to accept it and take back the extra or return all, whether he specified for each weight a dirham or not, because when the kind is the same, equality is necessary. End. And in Da'wa al-Bazzaziyyah: someone claimed a piece of silk its length is such and such according to the cubits of Khwarazm, and two witnesses testified accordingly in the presence of the silk seller; then he measured and found it more or less; the testimony and claim become void, as if the age of the she-animal contradicts the claim or testimony. And their statement: the cubit is description, so it is disregarded in the present [case] in prices and sales, not in claim and testimony, because if they testify to a description and it appears contrary, it is not accepted. And he also mentioned: someone claimed iron indicating it and mentioned that it is ten manns; and it turned out to be twenty or eight; the claim and testimony are accepted because weight in the indicated item is irrelevant. End.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the ruling of selling by the cubit (al-dhira'). The matn states that if a buyer says 'each cubit for such price' and the actual number of cubits is less, the buyer has the option to either take it at a reduced price or cancel the sale. If it is more, the buyer takes it all. The commentator explains that the cubit is initially a description (sifah), but when assigned a separate price, it becomes a principal (asl) and rises from subordination. Therefore, if the quantity is less, the buyer has a choice because otherwise he would not be paying the specified per-unit price. If the quantity is more, the increase does not automatically belong to the buyer because the cubit is treated as a principal, so the buyer has the option to either take the increase for its portion or cancel. The commentator addresses an objection suggesting the contract should be invalid in case of shortfall, similar to selling two Herawi cloths that turn out to be Marwi, but distinguishes that the cubit retains some descriptiveness. He also distinguishes from the case of a heap (sibrah) where the increase does enter the contract. The discussion then expands to measured items (madhru'at) like land and cloth, and weighed items (mawzunat) where division harms the item (e.g., gold ingots, manufactured goods). The ruling differs based on whether the weight is considered description or quantity. Finally, examples from judicial practice (al-Bazzaziyyah) show that in claims and testimony, if the described quantity differs, the testimony is void for length but not for weight if the item is pointed to, because weight is disregarded in such cases. The lesson highlights the nuanced treatment of description vs. principal in Hanafi sales law.

Key Terms
ذُراع (dhurāʿ): A unit of length used for measuring cloth, land, etc.; here it is the unit of measurement in the sale.
وَصْف (waṣf): A quality or attribute of the sold item, such as length or weight; here it distinguishes between a description that is merely incidental vs. one that is treated as a principal component.
أَصْل (aṣl): A principal or independent component of the sale, as opposed to a mere description; here the cubit becomes an aṣl when priced individually.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says 'I sell you this cloth, each cubit for 2 dirhams' and the cloth is found to be 12 cubits instead of the believed 10, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi madhhab?
A) The buyer must take all 12 cubits for the original total price of 20 dirhams.
B) The buyer may take all 12 cubits and pay for the additional 2 cubits at the per-unit rate (2 dirhams each).
C) The buyer has the option to take the increase for its portion or cancel the sale.
D) The sale is invalid because the quantity differs.

Key Takeaway
The per-unit pricing transforms a description (waṣf) into a principal (aṣl), giving the buyer options in case of quantity discrepancy, a uniquely Hanafi compromise between flexibility and contractual certainty.

The Sale of Ten Cubits from a House: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Linguistic Interpretation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on linguistic interpretation in sale contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the sale of ten cubits from a house without shares and explain how the interpretation of the contractual phrase (muʾaddā al-tarkīb) determines the ruling.

Core Idea
The sale of ten cubits from a house is corrupt according to Abu Hanifa but valid according to the Sahibayn—dispute turns on linguistic interpretation.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of selling a specific number of cubits from a house without specifying shares. The difference hinges on how the phrase 'ten cubits from a house' is understood. Abu Hanifa holds it implies a specific location, leading to invalidity due to potential dispute. The Sahibayn interpret it as a common share, which is valid by consensus. Understanding this case sharpens your ability to analyze contractual language in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed transaction
Recognize that the contract involves selling a specific number of cubits (length) from a house, not a fractional share. The buyer does not acquire an undivided portion but a measurable area.
The key term is 'without shares' (lā ashum), meaning the seller does not specify a fraction like 1/10.
2
Analyze the two interpretations of the phrase
Abu Hanifa interprets 'ten cubits from a house' as a specific measured area, implying a particular location. The Sahibayn interpret it as a common share (shāʾiʿ), similar to saying 'ten shares' of the house.
The basis of difference is muʾaddā al-tarkīb – the import of the linguistic construction.
3
Trace the ruling from each interpretation
Abu Hanifa: because the phrase indicates a specific measure and the parts of a house vary in quality, a dispute over location arises, corrupting the sale (fasid). Sahibayn: since it is treated as a share, selling a common share is valid by consensus, so the sale is valid (jaʾiz).
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the contract is enforceable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفسد بيع عشرة أذرع من دار لا أسهم وهذا عند أبي حنيفة . وقالا : هو جائز كما لو باع عشرة أسهم من دار . ومبنى الخلاف في مؤدى التركيب؛ فعندهما كأنه شائع باع عشر وبيع الشائع جائز اتفاقاً، وعنده مؤداه قدر معين والجوانب مختلفة الجودة فتقع المنازعة في تعيين مكان العشرة فيفسد البيع، فلو اتفقوا على مؤداه لم يختلفوا فهو نظير اختلافهم في نكاح الصائبة فالشأن مائة في رده
And the sale of ten cubits from a house without shares is corrupt, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is valid, just as if he sold ten shares of a house. The basis of the difference lies in the import of the construction; according to them, it is as if he sold a common share, and selling a common share is agreed upon to be valid. According to him, its import is a specific measure, and the sides are of different quality, so a dispute arises in determining the location of the ten, thus the sale becomes corrupt. If they agreed on its import, they would not differ. It is similar to their difference regarding marriage of the lost woman (nikah al-ṣa'ibah). The matter is one hundred in its return [؟].
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the sale of ten cubits from a house where the shares are not specified (i.e., the buyer does not buy a fractional share but a specific length). Abu Hanifa rules that such a sale is corrupt (fasid) because the phrase 'ten cubits from a house' implies a specific location, and since the parts of a house vary in quality (e.g., front vs. back), the exact ten cubits cannot be determined without dispute, leading to invalidity. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) analogize it to selling 'ten shares' from a house, which is valid by consensus, treating the ten cubits as a common share (shayi'). The essential difference lies in their interpretation of the phrase: the Sahibayn see it as a sale of a portion (shayi'), while Abu Hanifa sees it as a sale of a specified quantity of space, which requires precise location. As a parallel, the text mentions their difference in the case of 'nikah al-ṣa'ibah' (marriage of a lost woman), where similar interpretive issues arise. The last phrase 'فالشأن مائة في رده' is unclear but likely refers to the principle being analogous.

Key Terms
شَائِع (shāʾiʿ): A common share or undivided portion of property; in this context, the Sahibayn treat the ten cubits as a shāʾiʿ share.
مُؤَدَّى التَّرْكِيب (muʾaddā al-tarkīb): The import or interpretation of the linguistic construction; the basis of the dispute is how the phrase 'ten cubits from a house' is understood.
صَائِبَة (ṣāʾibah): A lost woman (wife missing); reference to a parallel dispute regarding marriage of a woman whose whereabouts are unknown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is the sale of ten cubits from a house without shares considered corrupt?
A) Because the seller cannot own ten cubits separately.
B) Because the phrase indicates a specific location and the parts differ in value, causing potential dispute.
C) Because the buyer cannot take possession of ten cubits.
D) Because house cubits are not standardized.

Key Takeaway
The validity of selling a portion of property depends on whether the phrase is interpreted as a specific measure or a common share within the Hanafi school.

Rulings on Sale by Measure and Weight with Quantity Conditions
Commentary expanding rules of sale by measure and weight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the validity of a sale when the measured quantity differs from the condition and identify the buyer's option rights depending on how the price was set.

Core Idea
When quantity is a condition but not a separate price, increase goes to buyer gratis; decrease gives option.

When you buy land, cloth, or a gold ingot with a stated measure or weight, the actual quantity may differ. The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between cases where the total price is lump sum versus priced per unit. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the buyer's rights and the extension of these rules to items that cannot be split without damage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of condition
Determine whether the sale specifies a lump sum price for a total measure (e.g., 'this land for 1000 on condition it is 1000 cubits') or a per-unit price (e.g., 'each cubit for 1 dinar').
The ruling changes based on this distinction.
2
Apply the lump sum rule
If lump sum and measure differs: if more, buyer takes increase without option; if less, buyer has option to accept reduced or rescind.
The increase is considered a gift or description; the decrease is a defect.
3
Apply the per-unit price rule
If per-unit price and measure differs: if more, buyer has option to pay extra or withdraw; if less, price reduces proportionately.
Option exists because variation affects total price.
4
Extend to weighed items that cannot be split
Identify items where splitting damages the remainder (e.g., a gold ingot, a brass statue). The same rule applies: weight is treated as a description.
The illa (effective cause) is that splitting causes defect, making weight a description.
5
Apply special cases for same-genus sales and testimony
For same-genus sales (e.g., silver with silver), equality is required; any increase voids the sale if discovered after possession. In testimony, specified measure/weight is binding; if contradictory, testimony fails—unless the item is pointed to (مشار إليه) where the value is merely descriptive.
These nuances protect contracts and evidence.

أطلق في المذروع فشمل الثوب والأرض والحطب والدار، فلو قال بعتك هذه الأرض على أنها ألف ذراع بألف فوجدها زائدة أو ناقصة فالبيع صحيح وله الزيادة بلا خيار وله الخيار مع النقصان . وإن أفرد لكل ذراع ثمناً . خير في صورة الزيادة وسقطت حصة النقصان ؛ كذا في البدائع. قال: وعلى هذا الموزونات التي في تبعيضها ضرر بأن قال بعت منك هذه السبيكة من الذهب على أنها مثقالان بكذا جاز البيع، فإن وجدها أزيد أو أنقص فهو كالمذروعات، وكذا إذا باع مصوغاً من نحاس أو صفر فهو على هذا التفصيل المذكور لأن الوزن في مثله يكون ملحقاً بالصفة لأن تبعيضه يوجب تعييب الباقي وهذا حد الصفة. ولو باع مصوغاً من الفضة وزنه مائة بدنانير ولم يسم لكل عشرة ثمناً على حدة وتقابضا جاز، فإن وجده أزيد فالكل للمشتري، وإن وجده أقل لكل عشرة ثمناً على حدة بأن قال وكل وزن عشرة بدينار، فإن وجده أزيد، خير، وإن سمى فإن علم قبل التفرق خير إن شاء زاد في الثمن وإن شاء ترك. وإن علم بعده بطل بقدر الزيادة وله الخيار فيما بقي لأن الشركة فيه عيب، وإن وجده ناقصاً خير قبل التفرق وبعده إن شاء وإن شاء رضي به بقسطه من الثمن. وكذا لو باع مصوغاً من ذهب بدراهم فهو على هذا التفصيل، ولو باع مصوغاً بجنسه مثل وزنه فوجده أزيد فإن علم بها قبل التفرق فله الخيار إن شاء زاد في الثمن قدرها وإن شاء ،ترك، وإن علم بها بعد التفرق بطل لفقد القبض في قدرها، وإن وجده أقل فله الخيار إن شاء رضي به واسترد الفضل وإن شاء رد الكل، سواء سمى لكل وزن درهم درهماً أو لا، لأن عند اتحاد الجنس لا بد من المساواة اهـ. وفي دعوى البزازية : ادعى زندبيجاً طوله بذرعان خوارزم كذا وشهدا بذلك كذلك بحضرة الزندبيجي فذرع فإذا هو أزيد أو أنقص بطلت الشهادة والدعوى كما إذا خالف سن الدابة الدعوى أو الشهادة. وقولهم الذرع وصف فيلغو في الحاضر ذلك في الأثمان والبيع لا في الدعوى والشهادة فإنهما إذا شهدا بوصف فظهر بخلافه لم يقبل . وذكر أيضاً : ادعى حديداً مشاراً إليه وذكر أنه عشرة أمناء فإذا هو عشرون أو ثمانية تقبل الدعوى والشهادة لأن الوزن في المشار إليه لغو اهـ
It is general in what is measured by cubit, so it includes cloth, land, firewood, and house. If one says 'I sold you this land on the condition that it is one thousand cubits for one thousand,' and he finds it more or less, the sale is valid, and he gets the increase without option, and he has the option with the decrease. If he assigns a price for each cubit, he has the option in the case of increase, and the share of the decrease falls. So in al-Bada'i. He said: And upon this are the weighed items whose splitting causes damage, such as if he says 'I sold you this ingot of gold on the condition that it is two mithqals for such-and-such,' the sale is valid. If he finds it more or less, it is like measured items. Similarly, if he sells a manufactured item of copper or brass, it follows this detailed ruling because weight in such cases is attached to the description, since splitting it causes defect in the remainder, and this is the definition of description. If he sells a manufactured item of silver weighing one hundred for dinars and does not name a price for each ten separately and they take possession, it is valid. If he finds it more, all belongs to the buyer. If he finds it less, for each ten separately by saying 'and each weight of ten for a dinar,' if he finds it more, he has option. If he names and knows before separation, he has option: if he wishes he increases the price and if he wishes he leaves. If he knows afterwards, it becomes void for the amount of the increase and he has option for what remains because partnership in it is a defect. If he finds it less, he has option before and after separation: if he wishes he accepts it and takes back the excess, if he wishes he returns all. Similarly, if he sells a manufactured item of gold for dirhams, it follows this detail. If he sells a manufactured item of the same genus like its weight and finds it more, if he knows before separation he has option: if he wishes he increases the price by its amount and if he wishes he leaves. If he knows after separation, it becomes void due to lack of possession in that amount. If he finds it less, he has option: if he wishes he accepts it and takes back the excess, if he wishes he returns all, whether he named each weight dirham by dirham or not, because when the genus is unified, equality is required. End. And in the دعوى البزازية: He claimed a zandabij whose length by two Khwarazm cubits is such, and two witnesses testified accordingly in the presence of the zandabij, and it was measured and found more or less, the testimony and claim are invalid, just as if the age of the animal contradicts the claim or testimony. And their statement that measurement is a description is void in the present, that regarding prices and sales, not in claims and testimony, because if they testify to a description and contrary appears, it is not accepted. And he also mentioned: He claimed iron pointed to and mentioned that it is ten manns, and it turned out to be twenty or eight, the claim and testimony are accepted because weight in the pointed-to item is void.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings of selling by measurement (مذروع) and weight (موزون). The author begins by stating that the ruling for measured items (مذروع) applies generally to cloth, land, firewood, and houses. The key principle: if a person sells land specifying a certain number of cubits for a lump sum, and the actual measure is found to be different, the sale remains valid. If it is more, the buyer takes the increase without any option to reject; if it is less, the buyer has the option to accept the lesser quantity or rescind the sale. However, if the seller prices each cubit separately, then in case of increase the buyer has an option (to pay for the extra or withdraw), and in case of decrease the price is reduced proportionately. This is from al-Bada'i. The author then extends the same rule to weighed items that cannot be split without damage (such as ingots or manufactured items made of copper, brass, etc.). The reasoning is that weight in such items is treated as a description (صفة), not as a separate component, because splitting the item would cause defect. For example, selling an ingot of gold as two mithqals: if found more or less, it follows the same rule as measured items. Then the passage details the scenario of selling a manufactured silver item for dinars: if the price is per total weight and no price per unit is named, the buyer takes all if found heavier; if lighter, the buyer has option. If the price is per unit (e.g., each ten weight for a dinar), then on finding increase, the buyer has option before separation; after separation, the sale is void for the excess and the buyer has option for the remainder. On finding decrease, the buyer has option both before and after separation. Similarly for gold items sold for dirhams. A special case is when selling an item of the same genus by weight: equality is required; any increase requires option before separation but voids the sale after separation. The passage concludes with a note from دعوى البزازية about claims and testimony: if a claimant specifies a measured quantity that contradicts the actual measurement, the testimony is rejected because the description is considered لغو (irrelevant) in present transactions but not in claims; however, for a pointed-to object (like a specific piece of iron), mentioning weight is irrelevant and testimony is still valid.

Key Terms
المذروع (al-madhrūʿ): Items sold by measure of length (cubits) such as cloth, land, etc.
الموزونات التي في تبعيضها ضرر (al-mawzūnāt allatī fī tabʿīḍihā ḍarar): Weighed items whose splitting causes damage, e.g., gold ingots, manufactured goods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a seller sells a copper statue with the condition 'it weighs 10 kilograms for 5000 dirhams' (lump sum), and it is found to weigh 9 kilograms, what is the buyer's right?
A) The sale is void because the condition is not met.
B) The buyer must pay the full price and accept the less weight.
C) The buyer has the option to accept the statue and pay a proportionate price or rescind the sale.
D) The buyer must pay an extra amount to compensate for the missing weight.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when a quantity condition is attached as a description in a lump sum sale, increase is gratis; only decrease gives option; per-unit pricing gives option for both increase and decrease.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Selling Ten Cubits from a House Without Shares
Commentary on a matn phrase explaining the intra-Hanafi dispute and its linguistic basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on selling a specified measure from a house and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A sale is void if the phrase implies a specific portion; valid if treated as a common share.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions on the sale of 'ten cubits from a house' without specifying shares. At stake is the legal interpretation of the phrase (mu'adda al-tarkib) and the resulting validity of the contract. We will examine the linguistic reasoning of each side and the practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and the intra-madhhab split
Note the matn phrase 'فسد بيع عشرة أذرع من دار لا أسهم' — this ruling is not unanimous. Know that Abu Hanifa holds invalidity (fasād) while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold validity.
The matn is citing Abu Hanifa's position.
2
Analyze the linguistic reasoning (mu'adda al-tarkib)
Abu Hanifa interprets 'cubit' (dhira') as a specific measurement, implying a designated portion of the house, leading to inevitable dispute over location. The two companions treat 'cubit' as a metaphor for an undivided share (shā'i'), which is saleable by consensus.
The disagreement is rooted in language, not in a different hadith.
3
Refute the misconception of al-Khassaf
The commentator explicitly rejects al-Khassaf's claim that Abu Hanifa only invalidates when the total number of cubits is not named. According to the correct view (as in al-Hidayah), Abu Hanifa's invalidity applies even when the total is stated.
This shows the importance of verifying the scope of a ruling.
4
Apply the dispute to practical scenarios
Under Abu Hanifa, the contract is fasid (void) and cannot be enforced; under the two, it is valid and the buyer becomes a partner in the house proportionally. Later Hanafi fatwa relies on the companions' view for ease of transactions.
The thamara al-khilaf: the buyer becomes a co-owner if valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وفسد بيع عشرة اذرع من دار لا أسهم وهذا عند أبي حنيفة . وقالا : هو جائز كما لو باع عشرة أسهم من دار . ومبنى الخلاف في مؤدى التركيب؛ فعندهما كأنه شائع باع عشر وبيع الشائع جائز اتفاقاً، وعنده مؤداه قدر معين والجوانب مختلفة الجودة فتقع المنازعة في تعيين مكان العشرة فيفسد البيع، فلو اتفقوا على مؤداه لم يختلفوا فهو نظير اختلافهم في نكاح الصائبة فالشأن في ترجيح المبنى هو يقول الذراع اسم لما يذرع به فاستعير لما يحله وهو معين بخلاف عشرة أسهم لأن السهم اسم للجزء الشائع فكان المبيع عشرة أجزاء شائعة مائة من سهم أطلقه فشمل ما إذا بين جملة الذرعان كأن يقول من مائة ذراع أو لم يبين. وبه اندفع قول الخصاف أن محل الفساد عنده فيما إذا لم يبين جملتها وليس بصحيح، ولهذا صور المسألة في الهداية فيما إذا سمى جملتها لكن اختلف المشايخ على قولهما فيما إذا لم يسم جملتها، والصحيح الجواز عندهما لأنها جهالة بأيديهما إزالتها. وقوله لا أسهم معناه لا يفسد بيع عشرة أسهم من دار وهو مقيد بما إذا سمى جملتها لأن عند عدمها يفسد البيع للجهالة لأنه لا يعرف نسبته إلى جميع الدار، فلو قال وفسد بيع عشرة أذرع من مائة ذراع من دار لا أسهم لكان أولى، ولفهم الفساد في الذرعان عند عدم التسمية للكل بالأولى ولكن اختصاره أداه إلى الإجحاف والحمام والأرض كالدار كما في البدائع. وفي المعراج : قال بعتك ذراعاً من هذه الدار ؛ إن عين موضعه بأن قال من هذا الجانب إلا أنه لا يميز بعد فالعقد غير نافذ حتى لا يجبر البائع على التسليم وإن لم يعين فعلى قول أبي حنيفة لا يجوز، وعلى قولهما يجوز وتذرع ، فإن كانت عشرة أذرع صار شريكاً بمقدار عشر الدار وبه قال الشافعي . ولو باع سهماً من دار فله تعيين موضعه. وذكر الحلواني أنه لا يجوز إجماعاً. وفي نسخة فيه اختلاف المشايخ على قولهما والأصح أنه يجوز؛ كذا في المغنى اهـ. وفي الخانية : ولو اشترى عشرة أجربة من مائة جريب من هذه الأرض أو عشرة أذرع من مائة ذراع من هذه الدار لا يجوز في قول أبي حنيفة
His statement: (And the sale of ten cubits from a house without shares is invalid) and this is according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is valid just as if he sold ten shares of a house. The basis of the disagreement is in the implication of the phrase: according to them, it is as if he sold a share (shāyiʿ) and the sale of a share is unanimously valid. According to him, its implication is a specific portion, and the sides have different quality, so dispute occurs in the location of the ten cubits, thus the sale becomes invalid. So if they agreed on its implication, they would not differ. It is similar to their disagreement in the marriage of the captured woman (nāṣibah). The matter is in preferring the basis. He (Abu Hanifa) says: 'Dhirāʿ' (cubit) is a name for the instrument of measurement, so it is used metaphorically for the measured entity, and that is specific, unlike ten shares because 'sahm' (share) is a name for a common part, so the sold item is ten common parts. He made it general, so it includes whether he states the total number of cubits, like saying 'from one hundred cubits', or not. And by this is refuted the statement of al-Khassaf that the invalidity according to him is only when he does not state the total; this is incorrect. Therefore, the issue is depicted in al-Hidayah as when he names the total. However, the mashāyikh differed regarding his (the two companions') view when he does not name the total; the correct view is that it is valid according to them because it is an ignorance that they have the means to remove. And his statement 'lā ashum' means that the sale of ten shares from a house does not invalidate, but it is restricted to when he names the total, because without it the sale would be invalid due to ignorance as he does not know its proportion to the whole house. So if he said 'and the sale of ten cubits from one hundred cubits of a house is invalid, not shares', that would be more appropriate, and the invalidity in cubits when the total is not named is understood by priority, but his brevity led to insufficiency. And bathhouse and land are like a house, as in al-Bada'i. And in al-Miʿrāj: He said 'I sold you one cubit of this house'; if he specified its location by saying 'from this side' but he does not distinguish afterwards, the contract is non-effective so that the seller is not compelled to deliver; if he did not specify, then according to Abu Hanifa it is invalid, and according to the two it is valid and it is measured. If it was ten cubits, he becomes a partner to the extent of one-tenth of the house, and al-Shafi'i said the same. And if he sold a share (sahm) of a house, he has the right to specify its location. Al-Halwani mentioned that it is invalid by consensus. In another version, there is disagreement among the mashāyikh according to the two, and the correct is that it is valid; so in al-Mughni. And in al-Khāniyya: If he bought ten jarībs from one hundred jarībs of this land, or ten cubits from one hundred cubits of this house, it is invalid according to Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya-style commentary) on the matn phrase 'وفسد بيع عشرة أذرع من دار لا أسهم' from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The commentator explains that this ruling—that selling ten cubits from a house without specifying shares is invalid—is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa only. His two companions, Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, disagree: they consider such a sale valid, just as selling ten shares (سهم) of a house is valid. The essence of the dispute is how the phrase 'ten cubits from a house' is understood linguistically and legally. Abu Hanifa argues that 'cubit' (ذراع) is a specific measure, so selling ten cubits implies a particular portion of the house, and since different parts of a house have different quality, this leads to potential dispute about which specific area the buyer gets, making the sale invalid due to gharar (uncertainty). The two companions, on the other hand, treat 'cubit' here as a metaphor for a share (شائع), similar to selling a share of the house, which is valid by consensus. The commentator then refutes al-Khassaf's claim that Abu Hanifa only invalidates when the total number of cubits is not mentioned; the correct view is that Abu Hanifa invalidates even when the total is mentioned, as depicted in al-Hidayah. The passage also discusses variations: selling a single cubit with or without specification, selling a share of a house, and includes the views of al-Shafi'i and others. The key principle is that according to Abu Hanifa, determining the exact location is impossible without further specification, leading to forbidden uncertainty. According to the two associates, the uncertainty can be resolved, so the sale is valid.

Key Terms
مؤدى التركيب (muʾaddā al-tarkīb): The implication of the phrase; what the combination of words leads to in meaning.
شائع (shāʾiʿ): An undivided share; a common part of a property.
فساد (fasād): Invalidity; a contract that is defective (fasid) is one that does not fulfill all conditions of validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), why is selling ten cubits from a house without specifying shares valid?
A) Because the buyer knows the exact location from the word 'cubit'.
B) Because the phrase 'ten cubits' is interpreted as selling an undivided share, which is permissible.
C) Because the seller must specify the total area, and here it is mentioned.
D) Because the price is certain and the contract is not deferred.

Key Takeaway
The validity of selling a portion of property without demarcation depends on interpreting the wording as a share versus a specific area; the relied-upon Hanafi position follows the companions' view for practicality.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Buying a Bundle with a Stated Count: The Ruling When Count Differs
Commentary on matn explaining the ruling for buying a bundle with specified count.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for buying a bundle with a specified count when the actual count differs, and apply the distinction between total price and per-piece pricing.

Core Idea
When buying a bundle with a stated count, a discrepancy invalidates the sale if the total price is fixed, but is resolved with option if the per-piece price is specified.

The Hanafi school carefully balances contractual certainty and fairness in sales. This lesson examines a common scenario: buying a bundle of identical items with a stated number. The ruling distinguishes between two pricing methods and explains how ambiguity affects validity. Understanding this distinction is essential for drafting valid contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling and scenarios
The passage considers a bundle of qīmī items (e.g., cloth) bought on condition it contains exactly ten pieces. Two scenarios: the actual number is less or more. Determine the ruling (fasid/batil) for each.
The core ta'lil (legal cause) is ignorance (jahl) of either the subject matter (mabī') or the price (thaman).
2
Trace the ta'lil for each scenario
Increase leads to ignorance of which ten pieces are sold (jahl fī al-mabī'). Decrease leads to ignorance of the price because the buyer must subtract the value of the missing piece, creating price uncertainty (jahl fī al-thaman).
When total price is fixed, both scenarios invalidate.
3
Examine the special case of per-piece pricing
If the price is specified per piece (e.g., 'each garment for 10 dirhams'), then decrease is valid because price is clear; buyer has option (khiyār) due to tafarruq al-ṣafqah (split transaction). Increase still invalidates because the extra piece makes the mabī' ambiguous.
This distinction is crucial for drafting contracts.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference and tarjih
A minority report from Abu Hanifa holds that even decrease invalidates. The commentator rejects this as not correct (ghayr ṣaḥīḥ), and the relied-upon position is that decrease is valid with option for the buyer.
The author's tarjih is based on clarity of price when per-piece pricing is specified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ومن اشترى عدلاً على أنه عشرة أثواب فنقص أو زاد فسد لجهالة المبيع في الزيادة وجهالة الثمن في النقصان لاحتياجه إلى إسقاط ثمن المعدوم. والمراد من هذه المسألة أنه اشترى عدداً من قيمي ثياباً أو غنماً كما في الجوهرة وقدمنا أنه لو اشترى أرضاً على أن فيها كذا نخلاً مثمراً فوجد فيها نخلة لا تثمر فسد البيع. وفي المغرب : عدل الشيء مثله من جنسه وفي المقدار أيضاً ومنه عدلا الحمل وعدله بالفتح مثله من وفي الخانية : لو اشترى غنماً أو عدل زطى واستثنى منه شاة أو ثوباً بغير عينه لا يجوز ولو استثنى واحداً بعينه جاز اهـ وفيها أحد الشريكين في الدار إذا باع بيتاً معيناً من الجملة لا يجوز كبيع نصف بيت معين شائعاً، وكذا لو باع من الأغنام المشتركة نصف واحد معين لا يجوز، وكذا لو كان بينهما أرض ونخل فباع أحدهما قطعة معينة من رجل قبل القسمة، ولو اختلفا في عدد الثياب المبيعة عند زيادته تحالفاً كما في الظهيرية قوله : (ولو بين ثمن كل ثوب ونقص صح بقدره وخير وإن زاد (فسد لأنه إذا قال كل ثوب بكذا فلا جهالة مع ولكن للمشتري الخيار لتفرق الصفقة عليه، ولم يجز في الزيادة لأن جهالة المبيع لا ترتفع به لوقوع المنازعة في تعيين العشرة المبيعة من الأحد عشر . وقيل عند أبي حنيفة لا يجوز في فصل النقصان أيضاً وليس بصحيح بخلاف ما إذا اشترى ثوبين على أنهما مرويان فإذا أحدهما مروي خلاف جنسه .
His statement: And whoever buys a bundle (ʿadl) on the condition that it is ten garments, and it decreases or increases, the sale is invalid, due to ignorance of the sold item in case of increase and ignorance of the price in case of decrease because he needs to drop the price of the non-existent item. The intended meaning of this issue is that he buys a number of consumable items (qīmiyāt) like clothes or sheep, as in al-Jawhara. And we have already presented that if he buys land on condition that it contains such-and-such productive palm trees, and he finds a non-fruitful palm tree, the sale is invalid. And in al-Mughrib: ʿAdl of a thing is its like in genus and also in quantity, and from it is ʿidlā al-ḥamal and ʿadluh (with fatha) meaning its like from... And in al-Khāniyya: If he buys sheep or a bundle (ʿadl) of Zutṭ garments and excludes from it a sheep or garment without specification, it is invalid; and if he excludes one specifically, it is valid. End. And in it: One of two partners in a house, if he sells a specific room from the whole, it is invalid, like selling half of a specified room as a share. Similarly, if he sells from the jointly owned sheep a specified single one, it is invalid. Similarly, if there is land and palm trees between them and one of them sells a specific piece to a man before division. And if they differ in the number of garments sold upon increase, they take an oath, as in al-Ẓahīriyya. His statement: (And if he specifies the price of each garment and it decreases, it is valid to the extent and he has option; if it increases, it is invalid. Because when he says 'each garment for such,' there is no ignorance, but the buyer has an option due to the division of the transaction on him, and it is not valid in increase because the ignorance of the sold item is not removed, since dispute occurs in determining the ten sold from the eleven. And it is said according to Abu Hanifa that it is invalid in the case of decrease as well, but this is not correct. Unlike if he buys two garments on condition that they are Marwī (a type of cloth), and one of them turns out to be Marwī of a different type.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage expands upon the matn phrase 'ومن اشترى عدلاً على أنه عشرة أثواب' from Kanz al-Daqaʾiq. The core ruling: if someone buys a bundle (عدل) of cloth with the condition that it contains exactly ten pieces, and it turns out to be more or less, the sale is invalid (فاسد). The reason is that in case of increase, the exact subject matter is unknown (which ten out of eleven?), and in case of decrease, the price becomes uncertain because the buyer would need to deduct the price of the missing item from the total. The author clarifies that the issue concerns items of value (قيمي) like clothes or sheep. He references al-Jawhara and previous discussion about land with productive trees. Then he cites al-Mughrib on the definition of 'عدل' (a bundle of similar items in genus and quantity). From al-Khāniyya, he adds that if someone buys a bundle and excludes an unspecified piece, it is invalid; but if the exception is specific, it is valid. He also relates similar rulings for partners selling a specific part of jointly owned property. The passage then addresses a variant: if the buyer specifies the price of each garment separately (e.g., 'each garment for such'), then if the number is less, the sale is valid for the actual number, and the buyer has the option (to accept or reject due to 'tafarruq al-ṣafqah'—the transaction being split across multiple items). If the number is more, the sale is invalid because the exact ten sold cannot be identified from the extra ones. Some reports attribute to Abu Hanifa that it is also invalid in case of decrease, but the author deems this incorrect, except in cases where the description is false (like buying two allegedly Marwī cloths and finding one of a different type).

Key Terms
عدل (ʿadl): A bundle of similar items (e.g., cloth or sheep) of equal genus and quantity.
قيمي (qīmī): Items that are not measured by weight or volume but by individual value (e.g., clothes, sheep).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer purchases a bundle of cloth as 'ten pieces for 100 dirhams' (total price). On delivery, eleven pieces are found. What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The sale is valid for ten pieces, and the extra piece is a gift.
B) The sale is invalid because the subject matter is uncertain.
C) The buyer has the option to accept eleven pieces for 110 dirhams.
D) The sale is valid, but the seller must refund the extra piece's value.

Key Takeaway
When buying a bundle with a specified count, the ruling hinges on how the price is expressed: a fixed total price leads to invalidity if the count differs, while a per‑piece price validates a decrease (with option) but not an increase.

Selling a Cubit vs. Selling a Share: The Hanafi Distinction
Explaining the validity conditions for selling a cubit vs. a share.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between selling a specific unit (cubit) and a common share, and state the conditions for a valid sale of each according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A cubit is specific; a share is common — ignorance of proportion invalidates the share sale, not the cubit.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author clarifies a subtle but critical distinction in sales of undivided property. When you sell a cubit of a house, you are selling a measurable length; when you sell a share, you are selling an unallocated fraction. The Hanafi school treats them differently. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the linguistic basis, and the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of sale
The text discusses selling a 'cubit' (dhirā') and a 'share' (sahm). Note that both are parts of a house, but they differ in legal treatment.
A cubit is a specific unit of length; a share is a common fraction.
2
Understand the linguistic distinction
The author explains that 'cubit' is a noun for the measuring instrument, then used metaphorically for what is measured; it is specific (mu'ayyan). In contrast, 'share' is a noun for a common part (juz' shā'i'). This drives the ruling.
This linguistic analysis is key to the Hanafi position.
3
Apply the condition for a share sale
Selling ten shares requires mentioning the total shares (e.g., out of 100) to avoid ignorance of the proportion. Without it, the sale is invalid due to gharar.
The condition is to specify the whole.
4
Analyze the cubit sale dispute
Abu Hanifa requires specifying the location of the cubit; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow it even without specification, making the buyer a partner proportionally. The passage inclines to the latter view.
The practical difference: with specification, the buyer gets a specific spot; without, they become a co-owner.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later mashayikh prefer the permissibility view of the two companions, supported by al-Hidayah and al-Mughni.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Source Text
