Inclusion of Rights and Appendages in Land Sale
Rulings on what is included in sale of land regarding rights and appendages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish which rights and appendages are automatically included in a land sale and which require explicit mention, and apply the Hanafi rules for validity.

Core Idea
Dependencies (marāfiq) follow the land; separate items need explicit mention.

When buying land, you often assume you get the road leading to it and the water channel. Hanafi fiqh confirms this, but also draws lines: some items like piled soil or graves are not included. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the details, helping you structure contracts correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sold object and its dependencies
Start by recognizing that the primary sold item is the land itself (bay' al-ard). Then note what counts as a dependency (tabi'): roads, water channels, and facilities (marāfiq) that are utilized with the land.
2
Understand the default inclusion rule
According to the Hanafi school, dependencies are included in the sale without explicit mention. The text states that mentioning 'rights' (huquq) or 'facilities' (marāfiq) is sufficient; one does not need both.
This is based on the principle: al-tābi' tābi' (the follower follows).
3
Apply the rule to specific examples
Consider the examples given: drinking right (shurb) is a dependency, so buying land with its drinking right is valid even if the measure is unspecified. Vines tied to stakes and buried pillars are included. Conversely, transferred soil gathered like a hill is not a dependency and is not included.
Each example illustrates the boundary between dependency and independent item.
4
Identify exceptions and items requiring mention
Graves and threshing floors are not considered dependencies; they are not included unless explicitly mentioned. Abu Hanifa ruled that selling a house with its courtyard is invalid because the courtyard is a separate entity, like combining a free man and a slave.
The exception shows that some items are so distinct they cannot be assumed to follow the land.
5
Consider timing and access rights
Rights enter at the time of sale, not before. A main road or non-through street is included automatically; a private road requires separate arrangement. If trees bought for cutting cause harm to land, the seller must compensate.
These nuances affect contract drafting and dispute resolution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والطريق ومسيل الماء والمرافق ما يرتفق به ويختص بما هو من التوابع كالشرب والمسيل. وقوله «كل قليل وكثير مبالغة في حق البائع في المبيع وبما هو متصل به اهـ. وظاهر ما في المجتبى أن ذكر الحقوق أو المرافق كافٍ ولا يحتاج إلى الجمع بينهما لإدخال الطريق والشرب. وقولهم أو مثلها تفسير لقولهم فيها ؛ كذا في المحيط فأحدهما يغني عن الآخر أيضاً. وفي الخانية : اشترى أرضاً بشر بها جاز البيع وإن لم يبين مقدار الشرب لأن الشرب تبع الأرض، فإذا كانت الأرض معلومة فجهالة التبع لا تمنع الجواز اهـ. وفي القنية : اشترى كرماً تدخل الوثائل المشدودة على الأوتاد المضروبة في الأرض، وكذا عمد الزراجين المدفونة في الأرض أصولها من غير ذكر . ولو باع أرضاً فيها تراب منقول من أرض أخرى لا يدخل في البيع إذا كانت مجموعة شبه التل ولو باع أرضاً فيها مقابر صح البيع فيما وراء المقابر. أشار إلى أنه لا تدخل أرض القبر في البيع. ومطرح الحصائد ليس من مرافق الأرض فلا يدخل في البيع بلا ذكر المرافق .اهـ. وفي المجتبى قال أبو حنيفة : باع داراً بفنائها لم يصح كمن جمع بين حر وعبد، وفي بيعها بحقوقها تدخل الحقوق وقت البيع لا ما قبله. وفي البدائع: الطريق الأعظم أو في سكة غير نافذة يدخل في البيع بلا تنصيص ولا قرينة، وإنما الكلام في الطريق الخاص في ملك إنسان فإذا كان يلي الطريق الأعظم فتح له باباً إليه وإلا استأجر الطريق أو استعاره. وفي البزازية : اشترى أشجاراً للقطع فلم يقطع حتى جاء الصيف، إن أضر القطع بالأرض وأصول الشجر يعطي البائع للمشتري قيمة شجر قائم جبراً.
And the road, water channel, and facilities are what is utilized and pertain to the appendages, like drinking [water] and watercourse. And his statement 'every small and large' is an exaggeration in the right of the seller regarding the sold item and what is connected to it. End. And the apparent [meaning] in al-Mujtaba is that mentioning the rights or facilities is sufficient, and there is no need to combine both to include the road and drinking [water]. And their statement 'or like them' is an explanation of their statement 'in them'; as in al-Muhit, so one of them suffices for the other as well. And in al-Khaniyya: if he bought land with its drinking [water right], the sale is valid even if he did not specify the measure of drinking, because drinking is a dependency of the land; so if the land is known, ignorance of the dependency does not prevent validity. End. And in al-Qunyah: if he bought a vineyard, the vines tied to stakes driven into the land are included, and likewise pillars of grapevines whose roots are buried in the land without mention. And if he sold land containing soil transferred from another land, it is not included in the sale if it is gathered like a hill. And if he sold land containing graves, the sale is valid regarding what is beyond the graves. This indicates that the land of the grave is not included in the sale. And the threshing floor is not among the facilities of the land, so it is not included in the sale without mentioning facilities. End. And in al-Mujtaba: Abu Hanifa said: He sold a house with its courtyard, it is not valid, like one who combines a free man and a slave. And in selling it with its rights, the rights enter at the time of sale, not before. And in al-Bada'i: The main road or in a non-through street enters the sale without explicit mention or indication; the discussion is only about the private road in the ownership of a person; if it adjoins the main road, he opens a door to it, otherwise he rents the road or borrows it. And in al-Bazzaziyya: He bought trees for cutting and did not cut until summer came; if cutting harms the land and the roots of the trees, the seller gives the buyer the value of standing trees forcibly.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings on what is included by default in a sale of land. The text discusses rights of way, water channels, and other facilities. The key principle is that rights that are dependencies of the land are included without explicit mention, but some items require specification. For example, a road and water channel are included as part of the land's facilities. The author notes that it is sufficient to mention either 'rights' or 'facilities' to include them. Buying land with a water right is valid even if the measure is unspecified because it is a dependency. In a vineyard, vines tied to stakes and buried pillars are included. Transferred soil gathered like a hill is not included. Graves are not included in the sale of land. Abu Hanifa's ruling that selling a house with its courtyard is invalid compares it to combining a free man and a slave in one sale, indicating a prohibition of combining separate entities. The main road or a non-through street is included without mention, but a private road requires access arrangements. In a case where trees are bought for cutting and summer comes, if cutting harms the land, the seller must pay compensation.

Key Terms
مرافق (marāfiq): Facilities or appendages attached to the land that are utilized, such as a water channel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when a house is sold 'with its rights' (bi-huquqiha), what is included?
A) Rights that exist at the time of sale only
B) Rights that existed before the sale
C) Both past and present rights
D) Only rights explicitly listed in the contract

Key Takeaway
Dependencies (marāfiq) like roads and water channels are automatically included in a land sale; non-dependencies (graves, soil piles) require explicit mention.

Inclusion of Buried Pillars of Grapevines in Sale
Ruling on inclusion of buried pillars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on inclusion of buried pillars of grapevines in a sale and apply the condition of being buried.

Core Idea
Buried pillars are included; placed ones are not—the fatwa turns on physical attachment to land.

Al-Ramli clarifies a dispute about whether pillars that support grapevines are part of the sale. The ruling depends on whether the pillars are buried in the ground or simply placed on the surface. This distinction reflects the Hanafi principle that items fixed to the land are considered part of it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the item
The item in question is 'amad al-zarajin' (pillars of grapevines), which are supports for the vines.
2
Note the condition
The crucial distinction is whether the pillars are 'madfuna' (buried, with roots in the ground) or placed on the surface.
Al-Ramli explicitly restricts the ruling to buried pillars.
3
Apply the fatwa from al-Qunyah
Based on al-Qunyah, the fatwa is that buried pillars are included in the sale; otherwise they are not.
Al-Ramli cites this as the relied-upon position.
4
Understand the rationale
Buried pillars are like part of the land due to attachment, while surface pillars resemble movable property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Al-Ramli said: Consider. His statement: 'exaggeration in the right of the seller [etc.]' Here there is omission and distortion. And the expression of al-Mujtaba is 'exaggeration in dropping the right of the seller from the sold item and what is connected to it.' His statement: 'And their statement 'or like them' is an explanation of their statement 'in them'' Apparently it is based on the narration of Hisham, not on what al-Hasan ibn Ziyad said, because according to him there is a difference between them, as passed in the previous statement. Look at what we wrote from al-Mujtaba there. His statement: 'The vines enter [etc.]' Al-Ramli said: 'al-watha'il' is the plural of 'wathal' with a harakah, which is a rope made of palm fiber, as in al-Qamus. His statement: 'And likewise the pillars of grapevines whose roots are buried in the land' He said: By 'zarajin' is meant the grapevine here. In Mukhtar al-Lugha: 'zurjun' with fathah means wine, and it is said the grapevine, a Persianized word. And by 'pillars' is meant what carries the branches of the grapevine in summer. And his restriction to 'buried' indicates that what is placed on the ground is not included, like wood placed in the vineyard. And the issue has become a point of fatwa. It is recommended based on what is in al-Qunyah to give fatwa of their inclusion in the sale if they are buried, otherwise not. Thus I saw in the handwriting of Shaykh al-Islam al-Shaykh Muhammad al-Ghazzi, may Allah have mercy on him. His statement: 'It is not included in the sale if it is gathered like a hill' In some copies: 'unless it is' with an addition of 'except' but what I saw in al-Qunyah is without it. His statement: 'So it is not included in the sale without mentioning facilities' Thus in most copies, and in one copy 'with mention' without 'not', and that is what is in al-Qunyah. His statement: 'And in al-Bada'i: The main road [etc.]' He mentioned similarly in al-Mujtaba and said: And likewise the right of water flow and the right of throwing snow in private ownership are not included except by explicit text or by mentioning rights or facilities. And if he did not mention rights, mention [the following]: And crops are not included in the sale of land without specification, nor are fruits included in the sale of trees except the portion that is cut. And if it does not harm, it is cut. And if he buys the trees absolutely, he has the right to cut from the root. If the seller claims that the buyer broke the branches of the trees, and the buyer says, 'I did not intend it, but it was unavoidable', then one refers to experts: if they say it is something that can be avoided, he is liable for the deficiency; if they say it is not avoidable, he is not liable for anything. And the humps are included in the sale of camels. And if another fish is found in the belly of a fish, it belongs to the buyer, and likewise ambergris found in its belly because it is seaweed in the sea, its food, and likewise everything that is the food of the fish. And in al-Sihah: 'marafiq al-dar' are the places of water and the like, and 'marfiq' of an affair is what one benefits from. End. And in al-Misbah: As for 'mirfaq' of the house, like the kitchen, latrine, etc., it is with kasr of the meem and fatha of the fa' only, by analogy with the name of the instrument, and its plural is 'marafiq'. End. And the blacksmith's bellows built from clay is Arabized. And in al-Qamus: the pack-saddle of the donkey is like 'kitab' and 'ghurab', and its 'wikaf' is its saddle-cloth; the saddler is its maker; and 'akafa al-himar' means he saddled it; and 'akkafa al-ikafa' means he made it. End. So it is explicit that 'ikaf' is the saddle-cloth. And the apparent meaning of the jurists' statement that it is different due to conjunction, but in al-Qamus in the chapter of 'ayn, 'bardha'a' is the mat under the saddle, without lam, and its dal may be dotted. End. So according to this, 'ikaf' is the saddle and 'bardha'a' is what is under it. But in custom, 'ikaf' is two pieces of wood above the saddle-cloth. And his statement 'without mention' is related to both issues. And in al-Khaniyya: A man ordered another to sell land containing trees; the agent sold the land with its trees; the principal said, 'I did not order you to sell the trees.' Al-Fadli said: The principal's word is taken regarding what he ordered, and the buyer takes the land with its share of the price if he wishes. And likewise if there was a building instead of trees. End. And in it: He bought a vineyard containing mulberry trees and rosebushes; on the mulberry trees there were mulberries and leaves, and on the rosebushes there were roses. He said, 'With every right it is his.' The mulberries and leaves of the mulberry are not included in the sale, and likewise the roses, because they are like fruit. End. His statement: 'And crops are not included in the sale of land without specification because it is attached to the land for separation, so it resembles the goods that are in it. And the analogy is not the fetus of the sold animal because what is meant is separation by the human, and the fetus is by Allah's grace, and because it is like a part due to homogeneity, unlike crops. He [the author] made it general, so it includes what has sprouted first, and he chose in al-Hidayah that it is not included if it has not sprouted because it is deposited in it. And it includes what has sprouted but has no value; there are two opinions without preference in al-Hidayah. And in al-Tajnnis he stated that the correct view is inclusion, as stated by al-Quduri and al-Asbijabi. And in al-Dhakhira he detailed: If it has sprouted at the time of sale, its inclusion is questionable; if it has not sprouted, it is definitely not included. Some corrected inclusion if its growth has advanced and it can be taken by hand; some corrected non-inclusion. And in al-Tatimma from al-Fatawa: The fatwa is that if it is green, it is not included; otherwise it is included. This is an excellent detail, and it is transmitted from al-Faqih Abu al-Layth. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: Fruits and crops are included in the sale of trees and land unless the buyer stipulates them. But this is anomalous, and in al-Hidayah he chose non-inclusion if it has not sprouted. His statement: 'So it includes what has sprouted first' meaning or not sprouted. He said in al-Nahr: Because then it can be taken by pulling. His statement: 'And he chose in al-Hidayah' meaning he chose non-inclusion in the case of not having sprouted. His expression: If the land is sold while its owner has sown it and it has not sprouted, it is not included because it is deposited in it like goods. His statement: 'And in al-Dhakhira he detailed' is a restriction of what he chose in al-Hidayah. And in al-Fath he transmitted like what is in al-Dhakhira from Fatawa al-Fadli and said: And al-Faqih Abu al-Layth chose that it is not ...
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This is al-Ramli's hashya (super-commentary) clarifying and refining the previous rulings. He begins by noting textual corruption in the phrase 'mubalagha fi haqq al-ba'i' and corrects it based on al-Mujtaba. He then explains that the interpretation of 'aw mithlaha' depends on the narration of Hisham versus al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, noting a difference. He defines 'watha'il' as ropes of palm fiber and clarifies that 'zarajin' means grapevine; the buried pillars of grapevines are included in the sale, while those placed on the ground are not, and this is the position for fatwa as per al-Qunyah. He discusses a variant reading in the text about soil gathered like a hill, noting a discrepancy between copies. He states that without mentioning facilities, certain rights like water flow and snow disposal are not included. He then addresses the issue of crops not being included in land sale, explaining that crops are attached for separation and thus resemble goods, not the fetus of an animal. He notes that al-Hidayah chooses non-inclusion if the crop has not sprouted, but there are differing opinions. Al-Dhakhira distinguishes: if sprouted at time of sale, inclusion is questionable; if not sprouted, definitely not included. Some scholars prefer inclusion if the crop has advanced growth. Al-Fatawa gives a fatwa based on whether the crop is green. The passage also mentions that fruits are not included in tree sale, and gives details on liability for broken branches. It then defines various terms like 'marafiq', 'ikaf', 'bardha'a', and presents a case from al-Khaniyya on agency. Finally, it discusses the inclusion of humps in camel sales and fish in fish bellies.

Key Terms
الزراجين (al-zarājīn): Pillars that support grapevines.
مدفونة (madfūna): Buried, with roots in the ground.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Ramli, what is the fatwa on the inclusion of pillars of grapevines in a sale?
A) They are always included regardless of placement.
B) They are included only if they are buried in the ground.
C) They are never included unless explicitly mentioned.
D) They are included only if the contract mentions 'huquq'.

Key Takeaway
Only buried pillars of grapevines are included in a sale; surface pillars are not.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi Dispute on Inclusion of Crops in Land Sale
Intra-Hanafi dispute on crop inclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the differing Hanafi views on inclusion of crops in a land sale and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
There is no single Hanafi view on crops; the fatwa distinguishes green (not included) from dried (included).

Al-Ramli surveys a major intra-Hanafi dispute: when land is sold with crops growing on it, are the crops included? The general rule is that crops are not included, but there are detailed exceptions. The preferred fatwa, transmitted from al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, distinguishes based on whether the crop is green or ready to harvest.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
The default Hanafi position is that crops are not included in a land sale unless specified, because they are considered separate goods deposited in the land.
This is based on al-Hidayah and other sources.
2
Note the exception for un-sprouted crops
If the crop has not yet sprouted, it is definitely not included, as it is like goods deposited (al-Hidayah).
3
Understand the detailed views for sprouted crops
There is a dispute: some say if sprouted and green, not included; if dried, included. Al-Dhakhira questions inclusion if sprouted at time of sale.
The fatwa from al-Fatawa is that green crops are not included, dried crops are included.
4
Recognize the anomalous view
Al-Jami' al-Saghir states that crops and fruits are included unless stipulated otherwise, but this is considered shadhdh (anomalous).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon fatwa is from al-Fatawa, transmitted from al-Faqih Abu al-Layth: if the crop is green, it is not included; if it is not green (dried/harvestable), it is included.
This is praised as 'tafsil fi ghayat al-husn' (an excellent detail).

Source Text

قال الرملي : فتأمل. قوله : (مبالغة في حق البائع الخ هنا سقط وتحريف وعبارة المجتبى مبالغة في إسقاط حق البائع عن المبيع وعما هو متصل به قوله : (وقولهم أو منها تفسير لقولهم فيها) الظاهر أنه مبني على رواية هشام لا على ما قاله الحسن بن زياد إذ عنده بينهما فرق كما مر في آخر القولة السابقة، وانظر ما كتبناه عن المجتبى هناك قوله : (تدخل الوثائل الخ قال الرملي الوثائل جمع وثل محركة وهو الحبل من الليف كما في القاموس. قوله : (وكذا عمد الزراجين المدفونة أصولها في الأرض) قال : المراد بالزراجين الكرم هنا. قال في مختار اللغة: الزرجون بالتحريك الخمر وقيل الكرم فارسية معربة. وأراد بالأعمدة ما يحمل عليها الثلج في ملك خاص لا يدخل إلا نصاً أو بذكر الحقوق أو المرافق، ولو لم يذكر الحقوق ذكر ولا يدخل الزرع في بيع الأرض بلا تسمية ولا يدخل الثمر في بيع الشجر إلا هو الصدر: قيمة مقطوع. وإن لم يضر بواحد قطع . وإن اشترى الشجر مطلقاً له القطع من الأصل. ادعى البائع على المشتري كسر أغصان الأشجار وقال المشتري ما تعمدت ولكنه ما كان بد منه يرجع فيه إلى أهل العلم به ; إن قالوا إنه مما يمكن التحرز عنه ضمن النقان، وإن قالوا مما لا يمكن لم يضمن شيئاً، وتدخل الأقتاب في بيع الجمال. ولو وجد في بطن السمكة سمكة أخرى كانت للمشتري وكذا العنبر الموجود في بطنها لأنه حشيش في البحر طعامها، وكذا كل ما كان غذاء للسمك. وفي الصحاح مرافق الدار مصاب الماء ونحوها، والمرفق من الأمر ما ارتفقت وانتفعت به اهـ. وفي المصباح: وأما مرفق الدار كالمطبخ والكنيف ونحوه فبكسر الميم وفتح الفاء لا غير على التشبيه باسم الآلة وجمعه مرافق اهـ. والكور للحداد المبني من الطين معرب. وفي القاموس : إكاف الحمار ككتاب وغراب ووكافه بردعته والأكاف صانعه وأكف الحمار إيكافاً ووكفه توكيفاً شده عليه، وأكف الإكاف تأكيفاً اتخذه .اهـ. فهو صريح في أن الإكاف البردعة، وظاهر قول الفقهاء أنها غيره للعطف ولكن قال في القاموس في باب العين البردعة الحلس تحت الرحل وبلا لام وقد تنقط داله اهـ. فعلى هذا الإكاف الرحل والبردعة ما تحته ولكن في العرف الإكاف خشبتان فوق البردعة. وقوله بلا ذكر» متعلق بالمسألتين. وفي الخانية : رجل أمر غيره . ببيع أرض فيها أشجار فباع الوكيل الأرض بأشجارها فقال الموكل ما أمرته ببيع الأشجار قال الفضلي: القول للموكل فيما أمر والمشتري يأخذ الأرض بحصتها من الثمن إن شاء، وكذا لو كان مكان الأشجار بناء .اهـ. وفيها : اشترى كرماً فيها أشجار الفرصاد وشجر الورد وعلى شجر الفرصاد توت وأوراق وعلى شجر الورد ورد وقال بكل حق هو له لا يدخل التوت وأوراق الفرصاد في البيع، وكذا الورد لأنه بمنزلة الثمر اهـ . قوله : (ولا يدخل الزرع في بيع الأرض بلا تسمية لأنه متصل بالأرض للفصل فشابه المتاع الذي هو فيها، ولا يرد حمل المبيع لأن المراد فصل الآدمي والحمل بفضل الله تعالى، ولأنه كالجزء للمجانسة بخلاف الزرع أطلقه فشمل ما إذا نبت أولاً واختاره في الهداية لأنه مودع فيها. وشمل ما إذا نبت ولم يصر له قيمة وفيه قولان من غير ترجيح في الهداية. وصرح في التجنيس بأن الصواب الدخول كما نص عليه القدوري والأسبيجابي. وفصل في الذخيرة فقال: إن نبت وقت البيع ففي دخوله تردد، وإن لم ينبت فلا يدخل قطعاً. وبعضهم صحح الدخول مع تقدم نباته وإمكان أخذه باليد، وبعضهم صحح العدم. وذكر في التتمة عن الفتاوى أن الفتوى على أنه إن كان أخضر لا يدخل وإلا يدخل. وهذا تفصيل في غاية الحسن وهو منقول عن الفقيه أبي الليث. وفي الجامع الصغير: الثمر والزرع داخلان في بيع الشجر والأرض إلا أن يشترطهما المبتاع. ولكنه شاذ، وقد اختار في الهداية أنه لا يدخل فيما إذا لم ينبت. قوله : (فشمل ما إذا نبت أولا) أي أو لم ينبت قال في النهر : لأنه حينئذ يمكن أخذه بالغزل. قوله : (واختاره في الهداية) أي اختار عدم الدخول فيما إذا لم ينبت وعبارته : إذا بيعت الأرض وقد بذر فيها صاحبها ولم ينبت لم يدخل فيه لأنه مودع فيها كالمتاع. قوله : وفصل في الذخيرة الخ) تقييد لما اختاره في الهداية ونقل في الفتح مثل ما في الذخيرة عن فتاوى الفضلي وقال : واختار الفقيه أبو الليث أنه لا
Al-Ramli said: Consider. His statement: 'exaggeration in the right of the seller [etc.]' Here there is omission and distortion. And the expression of al-Mujtaba is 'exaggeration in dropping the right of the seller from the sold item and what is connected to it.' His statement: 'And their statement 'or like them' is an explanation of their statement 'in them'' Apparently it is based on the narration of Hisham, not on what al-Hasan ibn Ziyad said, because according to him there is a difference between them, as passed in the previous statement. Look at what we wrote from al-Mujtaba there. His statement: 'The vines enter [etc.]' Al-Ramli said: 'al-watha'il' is the plural of 'wathal' with a harakah, which is a rope made of palm fiber, as in al-Qamus. His statement: 'And likewise the pillars of grapevines whose roots are buried in the land' He said: By 'zarajin' is meant the grapevine here. In Mukhtar al-Lugha: 'zurjun' with fathah means wine, and it is said the grapevine, a Persianized word. And by 'pillars' is meant what carries the branches of the grapevine in summer. And his restriction to 'buried' indicates that what is placed on the ground is not included, like wood placed in the vineyard. And the issue has become a point of fatwa. It is recommended based on what is in al-Qunyah to give fatwa of their inclusion in the sale if they are buried, otherwise not. Thus I saw in the handwriting of Shaykh al-Islam al-Shaykh Muhammad al-Ghazzi, may Allah have mercy on him. His statement: 'It is not included in the sale if it is gathered like a hill' In some copies: 'unless it is' with an addition of 'except' but what I saw in al-Qunyah is without it. His statement: 'So it is not included in the sale without mentioning facilities' Thus in most copies, and in one copy 'with mention' without 'not', and that is what is in al-Qunyah. His statement: 'And in al-Bada'i: The main road [etc.]' He mentioned similarly in al-Mujtaba and said: And likewise the right of water flow and the right of throwing snow in private ownership are not included except by explicit text or by mentioning rights or facilities. And if he did not mention rights, mention [the following]: And crops are not included in the sale of land without specification, nor are fruits included in the sale of trees except the portion that is cut. And if it does not harm, it is cut. And if he buys the trees absolutely, he has the right to cut from the root. If the seller claims that the buyer broke the branches of the trees, and the buyer says, 'I did not intend it, but it was unavoidable', then one refers to experts: if they say it is something that can be avoided, he is liable for the deficiency; if they say it is not avoidable, he is not liable for anything. And the humps are included in the sale of camels. And if another fish is found in the belly of a fish, it belongs to the buyer, and likewise ambergris found in its belly because it is seaweed in the sea, its food, and likewise everything that is the food of the fish. And in al-Sihah: 'marafiq al-dar' are the places of water and the like, and 'marfiq' of an affair is what one benefits from. End. And in al-Misbah: As for 'mirfaq' of the house, like the kitchen, latrine, etc., it is with kasr of the meem and fatha of the fa' only, by analogy with the name of the instrument, and its plural is 'marafiq'. End. And the blacksmith's bellows built from clay is Arabized. And in al-Qamus: the pack-saddle of the donkey is like 'kitab' and 'ghurab', and its 'wikaf' is its saddle-cloth; the saddler is its maker; and 'akafa al-himar' means he saddled it; and 'akkafa al-ikafa' means he made it. End. So it is explicit that 'ikaf' is the saddle-cloth. And the apparent meaning of the jurists' statement that it is different due to conjunction, but in al-Qamus in the chapter of 'ayn, 'bardha'a' is the mat under the saddle, without lam, and its dal may be dotted. End. So according to this, 'ikaf' is the saddle and 'bardha'a' is what is under it. But in custom, 'ikaf' is two pieces of wood above the saddle-cloth. And his statement 'without mention' is related to both issues. And in al-Khaniyya: A man ordered another to sell land containing trees; the agent sold the land with its trees; the principal said, 'I did not order you to sell the trees.' Al-Fadli said: The principal's word is taken regarding what he ordered, and the buyer takes the land with its share of the price if he wishes. And likewise if there was a building instead of trees. End. And in it: He bought a vineyard containing mulberry trees and rosebushes; on the mulberry trees there were mulberries and leaves, and on the rosebushes there were roses. He said, 'With every right it is his.' The mulberries and leaves of the mulberry are not included in the sale, and likewise the roses, because they are like fruit. End. His statement: 'And crops are not included in the sale of land without specification because it is attached to the land for separation, so it resembles the goods that are in it. He [the author] made it general, so it includes what has sprouted first, and he chose in al-Hidayah that it is not included if it has not sprouted because it is deposited in it. And it includes what has sprouted but has no value; there are two opinions without preference in al-Hidayah. And in al-Tatimma from al-Fatawa: The fatwa is that if it is green, it is not included; otherwise it is included. This is an excellent detail, and it is transmitted from al-Faqih Abu al-Layth. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: Fruits and crops are included in the sale of trees and land unless the buyer stipulates them. But this is anomalous, and in al-Hidayah he chose non-inclusion if it has not sprouted. His statement: 'So it includes what has sprouted first' meaning or not sprouted. He said in al-Nahr: Because then it can be taken by pulling. His statement: 'And he chose in al-Hidayah' meaning he chose non-inclusion in the case of not having sprouted. Commentary
This is al-Ramli's hashya (super-commentary) clarifying and refining the previous rulings. He begins by noting textual corruption in the phrase 'mubalagha fi haqq al-ba'i' and corrects it based on al-Mujtaba. He then explains that the interpretation of 'aw mithlaha' depends on the narration of Hisham versus al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, noting a difference. He defines 'watha'il' as ropes of palm fiber and clarifies that 'zarajin' means grapevine; the buried pillars of grapevines are included in the sale, while those placed on the ground are not, and this is the position for fatwa as per al-Qunyah. He discusses a variant reading in the text about soil gathered like a hill, noting a discrepancy between copies. He states that without mentioning facilities, certain rights like water flow and snow disposal are not included. He then addresses the issue of crops not being included in land sale, explaining that crops are attached for separation and thus resemble goods, not the fetus of an animal. He notes that al-Hidayah chooses non-inclusion if the crop has not sprouted, but there are differing opinions. Al-Dhakhira distinguishes: if sprouted at time of sale, inclusion is questionable; if not sprouted, definitely not included. Some scholars prefer inclusion if the crop has advanced growth. Al-Fatawa gives a fatwa based on whether the crop is green. The passage also mentions that fruits are not included in tree sale, and gives details on liability for broken branches. It then defines various terms like 'marafiq', 'ikaf', 'bardha'a', and presents a case from al-Khaniyya on agency. Finally, it discusses the inclusion of humps in camel sales and fish in fish bellies.

Key Terms
الزرع (al-zar‘): Crops, cultivated plants.
أخضر (akhḍar): Green, referring to unripe crops.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi fatwa cited by al-Ramli, when are crops included in a land sale?
A) Always, unless the buyer stipulates otherwise.
B) Never, unless the seller stipulates inclusion.
C) Only if the crop is green and growing.
D) Only if the crop is not green (dried/ripe).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa on crop inclusion distinguishes green (not included) from dried (included).
